Mr. Rudolph: The Board of Zoning Appeals is an appointed seven member Board
established by State Legislature. It is given the responsibility to hear and act on all
appeals, requests for variances from the zoning code and establishment of special uses.
Since there are seven members of the Board of Zoning Appeals, to establish a quorum, we
must have four members present in order for a petition to be approved or denied. If you do
not have four votes to either approve or deny the request, you have the opportunity to go
before the Board the next month and be heard again. The denial of a petition for a
variance, special use, or an appeal by the Board of Zoning Appeals or the withdrawal of
such a petition by the petitioner shall prohibit the Board of Zoning Appeals from hearing the
petition for a variance, special use, or an appeal for the subject property or a part thereof
for 12 months from the date of the denial or withdrawal. An exception may be made upon
unanimous vote of the Board of Zoning Appeals. In granting a variance or special use, the
Board may set any conditions, requirements or limitations that it deems necessary and
which are appropriate to implement the principles and purposes of the zoning ordinance.
The Board keeps minutes of official action of its proceedings. These minutes and files are
public records and are kept in the Area Plan Commission office in Room 312 of the Civic
Center Complex. When you come before us, we ask that you state your name and
address into the microphone, since everything is recorded and kept as record.
This Board, which by State law, is a quasi-judicial body that cannot be contacted by the
public prior to the Board of Zoning Appeals hearings, has jurisdiction over two types of
petitions. One is special use and the other is variance. Neither of these categories is a
rezoning. They are special waivers or special conditions that this Board has authorization
to grant to the petitioner. A variance is an application to waive or modify certain
requirements of the Zoning Ordinance. It is not a rezoning of the property. In order to
receive approval, the following criteria must be satisfied.
The four conditions necessary to grant a variance are summarized as follows:
1.

The approval will not be injurious to the public health, safety, morals, and general
welfare of the community;

2.

The use and value of the area adjacent to the property included in the variance will
not be affected in a substantially adverse manner;

Board of Zoning Appeals
August 15, 2013
Page 3

3.

The strict application of the terms of the zoning ordinance will result in practical
difficulties in the use of the property;

4.

The variance is not a variance of the use of the property;

In our review of variance requests, the Zoning Code establishes the criteria that must be
applied to each petition. The Code specifically requires that these criteria must all be met
for a variance to be granted.
The second category that we have before this Board would be special uses. Certain uses
are necessary to the life and economic health of the community. But they have
characteristics of the operation that do not readily permit classification in the usual
residential, commercial or industrial districts. Special uses are secondary classifications.
They are not rezonings. In order for a special use to be approved, the following criteria are
used:
1.

whether the specific site is the appropriate location for the use;

2.

whether the use, as developed, will adversely affect the surrounding
area;
whether there will be a nuisance or a serious hazard to vehicles, pedestrians
or residences;
whether adequate and appropriate facilities will be provided for proper
operation of the use;

3.
4.

5.

whether the use is in harmony with the Evansville and Vanderburgh County
Comprehensive Plan; and

6.

whether the use is essential or desirable to the public convenience and
welfare.

The Board of Zoning Appeals approval or modification of a special use classification may
include whatever reasonable conditions, limitations, or temporary uses necessary for the
protection of the public interest.
To protect public interest and to ensure compliance with requirements to be included in the
site plan, the Board of Zoning Appeals may require whatever evidence and guarantees are
necessary to assure compliance with conditions, limitations, and temporary uses. There
will be a ten minute time limit for petitioners and then a 10 minute opportunity for
remonstrators. Following that, the petitioner will have five minutes for rebuttal.

Board of Zoning Appeals
August 15, 2013
Page 4

VARIANCES
Docket No: 2013-36-BZA Applicant: Ronnie & Patsy Thomason
Common Address: (Complete legal on file.) 5815 Millersburg Road
Nature of Case: Applicant requests relaxation of the restrictions of the zoning code to
allow temporary placement of a mobile home.
Mr. London: Ronnie and Patsy Thomason are requesting a renewal of their temporary
variance to relax the restrictions of the zoning code to allow temporary placement of a
mobile home. The Vanderburgh County code allows only one dwelling per lot in the
Agricultural district. In 2009, the Thomasons contacted Area Plan Commission regarding
reconstruction of their flood-damaged residence. At the time of the application, it was
noted by staff that there was an existing mobile home on the site, occupied by a sick
elderly parent of the owners. Area Plan Commission staff contacted the Thomasons with
an agreement, allowing the construction of their new home, subject to immediate removal
of the existing mobile home upon the demise of the mother who was residing in the mobile
unit. Since that time, Area Plan Commission staff was notified by the Building Commission
office that the existing Thomason house had received such extensive damage to its
foundation as a result of recent flooding that they had ordered the residence to be vacated
immediately for safety reasons, and all utilities were disconnected from the house as a
safety precaution. The Thomasons then moved into the existing mobile home on the site.
The existing residence has been demolished. In August of 2012, the Board of Zoning
Appeals approved a one-year time limit to allow the temporary maintenance of the mobile
home on the site. The Thomasons have obtained permit approval for their new home from
Area Plan Commission, and have been preparing their site for construction of their new
home. They had run into an issue with their septic system which has just recently been
resolved, and are preparing for their issuance of final building permits. They are requesting
additional time to work through the issues that they had encountered. It is recommended
by staff that the mobile home be approved only for the period of construction of the new
home. Once the Thomasons are able to move into their new home, the mobile home
should immediately be removed from the site or they will be in violation of the zoning code
for having two residences on one lot. This is a request for relaxation of zoning
requirements to allow for the temporary placement of a mobile home.

SPECIAL USES
Docket No: 19-2013-APC Applicant: Alan Ripplemeier
Common Address: (Complete legal on file.) 4116 Koressel Road
Nature of Case: Applicant requests a special use for a farm winery/vineyard
Mr. London: Alan Ripplemeier is requesting approval of SU-25 to allow establishment of
a farm winery in conjunction with his vineyard at 4116 Koressel Road. Mr. Ripplemeyer
has a 15 acre site located on the west side of Koressel Road, north of Marx Road. The
zoning code Chapter 17.28.050 requires approval of a special use permit (SU-25) by the
Board of Zoning Appeals for those uses identified in Use Group 19 in the zoning code. On
June 18, 2013, Vanderburgh County adopted a change to Use Group 19, adding ‚ÄúFarm
Products Processing and Sales - where fruits, vegetables, or other planted crops grown on
site are processed including but not limited to cooking, mixing with other ingredients,
bottling, packaging, etc. that transforms the fruits, vegetables, or other crops into higher
valued farm products for human ingestion (‚Äúvalue added farm products‚Äù). Such processing
may involve the making of wines, ciders, jams, jellies, and other consumable food or
beverage products.‚Äù The approval of this proposed farm winery requires SU 25 approval.
The proposed farm winery use requires parking spaces in an amount determined by the
Board of Zoning Appeals to be reasonably adequate to serve the public for customers,
patrons, visitors, and employees. The submitted site plan indicates a 15-space compacted
stone parking and access drive. Farm wineries and similar uses are further restricted by
ordinance as follows: 1. Written requests for temporary use of substitute crops grown off
site may be submitted to and approved by the APC Director upon the review of
documentation provided with the request of an unusually low on site crop harvest or other
special circumstances. 2. The sale of these value added farm products is allowed as
follows: a. The sale of other foods and beverages is allowed as long as these items are
associated with or commonly consumed with the value added farm product, are incidental
to the primary farm use, and do not involve cooking or preparation on-site; b. The sale of

Board of Zoning Appeals
August 15, 2013
Page 8

other incidental items commonly associated with the value added farm product or the farm
use is also allowed. 3. Facilities for the on-site processing, retail display, sales, and
sampling of value added farm products are allowed within the following parameters:
a. The facilities must be strictly ancillary and incidental to the primary farming use; b. The
facilities may include patio seating or other outdoor areas for picnics, agri-tourism
gatherings, private noncommercial gatherings hosted by the property owner or the farm
use operator, or other activities incidental to the farm use.

Nature of Case: Applicant requests a special use for a church and church-related
incidental facilities.
Mr. London: Living Hope Baptist Church is requesting SU-2 approval to allow
establishment of a church within the commercial building at 4925 Hitch Peters Road. The
petition filed by the church indicates that the church is requesting to lease the existing
commercial building one day each week, presumably on a day when the structure is not
otherwise in use by the owner Medic On-Site Services. The zoning code Chapter
18.145.050 requires approval of a special use permit (SU-2) by the Board of Zoning
Appeals for churches and church-related incidental facilities. There is an existing, partially
paved and partially graveled parking lot that was installed when the building was built in
1980. There are two paved access drives onto Hitch Peters Road, one at the south end of
the property, and one approximately 130 feet north of the south drive that leads to the front
of the building. The site plan submitted indicates approximately 106 parking spaces could
be available on the site within the area that is predominantly gravel. Space is available for
additional parking on site if it should become necessary for the use of the site. A church
requires 0.3 parking spaces for each seat in the church. Although no information has been
submitted regarding the proposed church attendance, the existing parking lot would
facilitate up to a 350-seat church, and there is space available on-site should the
congregation exceed that amount. Compliance with all code requirements will be
determined by Staff upon issuance of a Change of Business (occupancy) permit.

BOARD OF PARKS AND RECREATION
CONSOLIDATED CITY OF INDIANAPOLIS
March 20, 2014
The meeting of the Board of Parks and Recreation was called to order by Chairman
Williams, Thursday, March 20, 2014, at 3:45 p.m. Room 260, City-County Building, 200 East
Washington Street, Indianapolis, Indiana 46204.
Board Members Present:

Chairman, John Williams, Mr. Joe Wynns,
Josh Bowling and Anne Valentine

Staff Present:

Louvenia Holstein, Board Secretary
Suzanne Martin, Assistant Board Secretary
Doug Kowalski, Deputy Corporation Counsel

Staff Absent:

Dr. Jackie Greenwood

Approval of Minutes: None
Directors Announcements:
Chairman Williams greeted the Board and the audiance and he thanked everyone for being
there. Chairman Williams greeted the Board members and guests. Chairman Williams
stated that he has a couple of announcements. First and foremost, it is that time of the year
again where we at Indy Parks are looking for lifeguards for our pool season. Those of you
who are watching on television if you know someone who may be interested in becoming a
lifeguard this summer please contact the Indy Parks Department and we would be more than
happy to put you on staff. You have to know how to swim obviously, and be able to pass our
tests of rigourous training to become certified and we are looking forward to having a full
confident summer staff to help us open up our pools for a safe summer season.
Secondly we have been working on different kinds of promotions and there is a new one that
he believes is a good idea that if you want to support Indy Parks the Macy‚Äôs Department
store and the National Parks and Recreation Association have chosenBroad Ripple Park as
a location for what they call a new your park initiative through Macy‚Äôs. What this means is
you can go to the Glendale Macy‚Äôs location only and when you purchase items and
acknowledge that you would like part of the proceeds to go towards the project at Broad
Ripple Park. If you happen to find your way to Macy‚Äôs at Glenday Mall, please remember to
support Indy Parks. Thank you.
This is all Chairman Williams has as announcements and we do not have any minutes to
approve at this time and we will be approving last month‚Äôs minutes in April.

Agenda Item #4, 2014 ‚Äì The Resource Development Division is recommending that the
Board of Parks and Recreation support the Sons of Confederate Veterans in their efforts to
raise all funds necessary to restore the Garfield Park Confederate Prisoner of War
Monument.
Don Colvin greeted the Board and introduced Bryan Blevens and he has been able to have
the benefit to work with Brian on this project for quite a while now to work with his ideas and
what he is trying to accomplish and as we all know the Sons of Confederate Veterans
memorial down at Garfield Park has been there for a number of years and has fallen into
disrepair. The caulking joints are deteriating and in particularly the brass plaques are
needing aid and typically this is not something that the park agency have the resources to
make those repairs and particularly when we have leaky roofs, HVAC systems expenditures.
Brian came to him with an idea he would like to take on an opportunity to take on to fund
raise this and what we have here before you today seeking out the Board support to start
this initiative. They are not asking for any of the City‚Äôs dollars to be involved in this and he
will let Brian really speak to you of all the details. They have met with the Indianapolis Parks
Foundation president, Lori Hazlett and the foundation is more than happy to receive the
funds. They are not going to raise any additional funds for this project but they are very
much in support of receiving the funds and holding those funds until the time of the
expenditures and if there are any additional dollars left over from the fund raising process
those dollars will remain with the foundation for any future maintenance activities. If the
Board would so allow him he would like to turn the floor over to Brian to go over his
presentation to talk about what he is hoping to do for this war monument. Mr. Blevins
thanked Don and the Board for his opportunity to present his proposal to the Board. Brian
pointed to the first slide on the overhead screen noting that the monument is about 35 to 40
feet tall and about 20 foot wide. The monument has six bronze plates on its sides 3 on each
side. This monument, and of course that is him standing in front of it on the slide which
gives you a proportion of how big this monument is. The monument was errected in 1912 by
the United States Federal Government to honor the 1616 confederate POWs that died here
at Camp Morton here in Indianapolis during the Civil War. In the early 1920‚Äôs as the city
began to grow the Green Lawn Cemetary, presently the Diamond Chain Company became
in disrepaired so they disinteared every body located in the cemetary which included the
1616 confederate soldiers which took them about 3 years to finish the project and they
moved them out to Crown Hill Cemetary where they rest at this time.
In 1928 the Southern Club of Indianapolis asked the Parks Board to move the monument
while they were doing this disintearment of these veterans to Garfield Park as Garfield being
the only city park in Indianapolis at that time. Of course the Board approved the monument
to moved to Garfield Park. During the reintearment due to cost overuns and the great
depression that struck the United States, this monument was not moved due to the financial
costs that they could not afford, so it has been sitting in the park since 1928.
The condition of the monument is not bad for 102 year old monument. The stones are in
great condition. A lot of the caulking is missing and of course the brass plates are severely
weather worn with mold and in a bad state of affairs. The next picture on the overhead
screen shows the monument on the shady side and you can see all the black mold. The
picture on the right is a close-up of what the brass plaque will look like when restored.
2

With Mr. Blevins is Mr. Greg Hurrly, president of Hurrly Monument Company who has been
in business since 1999 and he has been asked to help them restore this monument. His
goal and request is to restore the monument for the City of Indianapolis public for the next
100 years. He is a member of the Sons of Confederate Veterans which is southern historical
society geared towards the preservation of the history and the heritage of their confederate
ancestors. Brian has received approval from the SCV to raise these funds for this projecrt.
He has obtained a quote from Mr. Hurrly to complete the project and he has been in contact
like Mr. Colvin stated with the Indianapolis Parks Foundation and they have stepped up and
agreed to hold the funds and distribute the funds for the expenditures of the repair and that
with any funds left over they will hold as future funds into an escrow account for future
maintenance expenses and there will be no burden on the City of Indianapolis or the tax
payers of Indianapolis for maintenance of this monument and they hope it last for a very long
time since the monument is in extremely good shape for a 102 year old monument.
Brian went on to tell the Board of his personal story. He stated that he is extremely excited
for the Board to give him the opportunity to make this restoration and thanked the Board for
allowing him to present to them his proposal. He is hoping that he will received the Board‚Äôs

Lastly, being a member of the Sons of the Confederate Veterans, people look at you in a

Ron thanked Andre and said he noticed that Andre is running for cover. Ron thanked
Director Williams, Deputy Director, Colvin and members of the Parks Board he appreciates
the opportunity to talk to you today. You received a hard copy of the Greenways Master
Plan document and hopefully you have had a chance to thumb through it. They are actually
really excited about this project and what he wants to do is take a few minutes to give you an
overview of what you are going to see in this Master Plan and give you a little bit of direction
because he knows that the amount of information in here can be a little bit intimidating so we
are going to step back a little and tell you a little about the process and how the
recommendations from this document came to be and then we are going to show you what
the Master Plan includes. He believes you will see why they are real excited about this.
When we think about the Greenways a lot of times we go back to the George Kessler Plan
which really was the first plan that really started to look at how we use some of our
recreational open spaces. If you look around the city today you can find pieces of that plan
still in place. There was a legacy that was left in the city by Kessler‚Äôs work but it is by no
means complete. This is still a vision that they are implementing today. On the overhead
screen is a photo of right before the winter began of the new construction happening on the
Fall Creek Greenway just to the west of the Monon Trail.
5

There has also been some contemporary planning done. The First Greenways Plan that
established the plan that is in place today was done in 1994, updated again in 2002, and it
too left a legacy, if you will, on the city. When we go out on a Saturday and we look at the
people that are walking along the Monon cooridor in Broad Ripple, this really is the legacy
that that plan has left. This vision as well has not been fully implemented and today we are
still implementing part of that system. This is an image on the overhead screen from the
South White River Greenway that‚Äôs construction is just currently rapping up on that. So he
thinks it is important to understand when we start this that what they are doing is establishing
the next vision, if you will, for where greenways need to go in the city, in the next 5 years, the
next 10 years, and the next 20 years and beyond.
Just to give you a little bit of background, our current system of trails and greenways, we
have just under 60 miles of greenway trails in the city. In the original or the plan from 2002
we still have about 44 miles that have not been constructed. Another key number that we
like to remind people of is the fact that we take user counts on all of our greenway trails.
Last year, or in 2012 we had over 3 million people use Indy greenways. These are some
significant recreational spaces. Their current system is broken into 10 separate greenways
cooridors and some are rail cooridors. Some are long waterways but we currently have 10 of
those different systems in place and this is what the current plan system looks like on the
overhead screen. They have bolded the redlines to show you what is currently in there from
the 2002 master plan. Now he is backing off a little bit and stated that the picture on the
overhead screen now is actually the graphic that shows just what has been built from that
plan. You are starting to see some things emerge when you look at this map. He is going to
add this yellow line in here and what this is is what they term as the service area of that
greenway and it basically is a half mile fringe on each direction from a built greenway and
that is roughly a 10 minute walk from a greenway. This starts to show us how many people
and how many geographic area within Marion County is within a 10 minute walk of our
greenways. Again, he thinks you can see that there is a pattern emerging and if you can‚Äôt
see it well lets change the graphic a little bit and take a look at the additional graph on the
overhead screen which depicts the map of Marion County and their townships and you can
see perdominately our greenways are developed in washington and center townships.
There are reasons for that with some of the early planning that went on, but we do have a
system today that is perdominately in those 2 townships. We also are living in a time in the
city that is much different than when the 2002 or the 1994 plans were done. What they are
seeing around the city now is we have an exploading bicycle culture. We are seeing many,
many miles of new on-street bike facilities such as the bike lanes and the emphasis on using
your bicycle to get around. There is an evolving health and fitness awareness as well as the
new transit initiatives that are happening across the city. There are initiatives out there to
reconnect to our waterways and there really is a growing resurgence in neighborhood
planning and development trying to figure out at the neighborhood scale we are starting to
plug into the city both the uniqueness of getting people to those neighborhoods as well as
how those neighborhoods can plug into the greenways system to be connected to other
things.
What they are doing with the full circle plan obviously trying to look at obviously some of the
improvements that are needed to that existing system but they are really establishing the
new vision for Indy Greenways and this is an important thing that we have to do because
6

completing this plan helps to ensure that the greenways are not only plugged into these
other initiatives and the regional transportation plan but also make sure that the greenways
are elegible for the different types of federal funding we seek to try to construct different
portions. We have been going through our planning process for a little bit over a year now
and he thinks this is probably something that is important for the Parks Board to understand,
and this is that this plan really has been driven by public engagement. It has been driven by
a level of public engagement that you don‚Äôt often see in plans like this. He wants to show
the Board some of those tools that they have used throught the past year and a half.
From the very beginning of the project they wanted to make sure that people were aware of
what was going on, what was happening with the plan, why they were doing it, what it was all
about so they began the process by having a series of promotional brochures printed and
distributed to libraries, community centers, schools, any place that would take a stack they
pretty much delivered those. There was also a project website established and this website
really is the portal, if you will, to this greenways plan. They have been able to put materials
on this website for the public meetings so that if people were not able to attend the public
meeting they have been able to direct them to the site and they are able to obtain the
information and know what has been going on. They have had a very active social media
platform. One of their tools that they have used the most has been their Facebook page that
is specific to the project and what this has really done has allowed them to connect with
several different people on a more intimate basis. Much more informal basis so that they are
able to strike up conversation about anything that might come up in the planning process.
Another unique thing that was done for this is that they opened a project office in Boulevard
Station, the historic rail depot is right where the monon meets 38 th Street and one day a
week the project development team and folks from his office would be staffed there where
people could schedule meetings and come in and talk to them, the neighborhood groups
could come in and talk to them, or if they just wanted to stop by and see what they were
working on they could sit down at the table and pull out some sketch paper and work with
them. They were pretty successful there in broadening the type of input we were able to get.
Incredibly they expected to get folks to come in with scribbled notes on notebook paper and
they got some of that but they also got some of this. People were coming in with their
neighborhood plans with ideas for what the trails could be, of how trails could connect and
where things could go and they think that this was really successful and they think that they
are starting to see that same model being replicated in some other processess going on in
the city. There also was an online survey conducted with residents and this was just a
facinating experience because what you are going to see in some of the recommendations is
driven by some of the things we received as part of this. He has blown this part up and he
thinks that one of the startling facts to them was that of the people who took the survey, 60%
of those people have to drive to get to a greenway. And if this isn‚Äôt startling enough, 49% of
the people who had to drive to a greenway had to drive more than 5 miles. So another way
that the same question was asked as seen on the bar graph on the right side of the
overhead slide asked the question of if you don‚Äôt use the greenways, why is that? 78% of
the people said because there is no greenway near their home or neighborhood. The data
that they received from this survey was pretty beneficial because it allowed them to start
bringing those types of things into their recommendations.

3:00 p.m.

PASTOR NICHOLS COSSEY and BEA JONES

CRYSTAL WELSH, BARKLEY GARRETT, DENNIS CORRELL, GARY

COLLIER, MIKE HUBER, HARRISON HAYNES and ROBBIN MILLER
(recording secretary)

Call to Order
The meeting was called to order at 3:00 p.m. by Mr. Eldridge, President.
Approval of December 11, 2012 Regular Meeting Minutes
Ms. Paolillo made a motion to approve the December 11, 2012 regular meeting
minutes, seconded by Mr. Eash; motion carried.
Approval of January 3, 2013 Organizational Meeting Minutes
Mr. Eash made a motion to approve the January 3, 2013 organizational meeting
minutes, seconded by Ms. Paolillo; motion carried.
Unfinished Business
There was no unfinished business for discussion.
New Business
a) Thompson Thrift ‚Äì Shoppes on Six

1

Mr. Garrett reported that as the Commission is aware staff has been working with
Thompson Thrift on the Shoppes on Six project. We are getting closer and closer to
where we need to be. A couple of months ago the Redevelopment Commission
authorized staff to work with Council to come up with an agreement that made sense for
both the development company and the City. Mr. Garrett believes that we are to that
point now. Representatives from Thompson Thrift are present to give a short
presentation and then discuss the draft agreement.
Mr. Ashlee Boyd stated that it felt good to be back in Elkhart. Thompson Thrift has been
working very closely with Mr. Garrett and his team to get to this point. They are excited
to be back before the Commission to refresh everybody on what they are attempting to
do.
Mr. Boyd explained that Thompson Thrift is proposing the expansion of the current
property that they own at Cassopolis and C.R. 6. Thompson Thrift is an Indiana based
company who has been around about 25 years. They have completed projects in 100
cities and 10 states. They have closed a significant number of new projects over the last
four years. They will complete a number of new projects on the horizon in addition to the
Shoppes on Six project. Thompson Thrift has a strong and diverse banking relationship
that will allow them to get projects like this done.
Mr. Boyd showed the Commission projects that Thompson Thrift had completed in
Carmel Indiana, Terre Haute Indiana, the Barnes and Noble Bookstore for ISU, LA
Fitness in Chicago Illinois and Cincinnati Ohio.
Shoppes on Six will consist of a unique and upscale shopping center destination
containing an exciting mix of first class retailers and restaurants. It will have a cohesive
up scaled landscaping design theme, unique upscale architectural design containing an
appropriate mix of brick masonry and other quality building materials. It will be truly a
first class retail project unique to Elkhart.
It will be approximately 20 acres and consist of approximately 115,000 square feet of
total space including the out parcels. Some of the offsite improvements that will be
performed, Thompson Thrift is proposing installing a signal at the west access drive,
separating their project from the Walmart. It will take you up to Lowe‚Äôs.
Thompson Thrift is projecting that a project of this size will create upwards of 200 new
jobs for the community, which is always exciting. Ultimately approximately $15 million
dollars will be invested in the project which will include Thompson Thrift‚Äôs investment
and the investment from the restaurants and the people who will ultimately occupy the
out parcels.
The project will be marketed and leased to regional, national and credit retailers and will
contain a complimentary mix of apparel boutique shops, jewelry, sit down and fast,
casual restaurants and other upscale uses commonly found in similar retail projects.
Thompson Thrift is working closely with Carmike Cinemas. Last time they were here
2

they spoke a little bit about that. They have had some dialogue with them since. They
have obtained construction estimates for the construction of their new facility and are
working with a group that will provide the financing for that. They are making progress
on that front which will be an exciting addition to the project. Thompson Thrift is
designing their project so that it will encompass the theatre redevelopment, however
that might take shape. Thompson Thrift does have a proposed site plan that would
accommodate the theatre.
Mr. Boyd showed a concept plan with the existing theatre and a concept plan with the
theatre option.
Tenants that Thompson Thrift is currently working with are TJ Maxx, Shoe Carnival, Pet
Smart and other shops.
Mr. Boyd encouraged everyone to visit their completed project in Warsaw, Indiana. It is
very similar to what they are proposing to do in Elkhart. The project in Warsaw is a total
of 175,000 square feet. The expansion that they completed is approximately 75,000
square feet. The project in Elkhart is approximately 80,000 square feet. It has proven to
be a huge success in Warsaw.
Mr. Boyd stated that their goal is to get this project on the ground in the summer of
2013, but they have agreed in their discussions with the Economic Development staff
that it will be no later than December of 2013. Thompson Thrift would like to get moving
on this project as soon as possible. Part of their challenge is making sure that they get
the appropriate retailer commitments in place.
Once they do start construction it will take approximately nine months to complete the
project from the day they put a shovel in the ground to the day that the first retailers are
open for business. It is a relatively short build period once it starts.
Mr. Boyd said they are working to complete the TIF and the project approvals. They will
commence with a complete project design once they solidify the economic development
agreement with the City and continue to work towards securing the pre-leasing
commitments and construction financing. Mr. Greg Buckhout is present who heads up
Thompson Thrift‚Äôs capital group. He is available to answer questions about that aspect.
As discussed in the last presentation, the project requires financial participation from the
City. Thompson Thrift has worked through the details of that agreement with the
Economic Development Department. They feel like they have a good structure in place.
Phase two of the expansion in front of the main shopping center will be at a cost of
$13.5 million dollars. Thompson Thrift is seeking a $3 million dollar investment by the
municipality by the City of Elkhart. Thompson Thrift will then fund the balance of the
$10.5 million dollars in cost.

3

The public investment is supported through a substantial increase in tax increment
created by the project. Thompson Thrift will only utilize the incremental taxes that they
are creating. They will not touch the existing tax bases that exist today with the
properties there.
The public investment will consist of three components: a twelve month bond issued
from existing Cassopolis TIF district. That bond will be purchased by Thompson Thrift
and be paid back using Cassopolis Street TIF district fund. The second component will
be a five year bond purchased by Thompson Thrift and paid back by incremental taxes
generated by just their project. The third component is an approximate five year loan
from the City, which will be paid back utilizing the tax increment from the overall
Cassopolis Street TIF district.
As mentioned before one of the commitments that Thompson Thrift has made, is that
this project will be 75% pre-leased before they issue a bond or put a shovel in the
ground. They want to make sure that this is a real project that is viable, and that there
are tenants and leases in place. Thompson Thrift is also providing a completion
guarantee as part of their agreement with the City so that the City can be assured that
once they start the project will be completed. If it is not completed, then Thompson Thrift
would have to stand behind that.
The next steps are that Thompson Thrift respectfully request the Commission‚Äôs
approval of the Economic Development agreement that will allow them to move on to
the Council level. They will then proceed with completing their due diligence and
wrapping up their pre-leasing commitments and finalizing the project.
Mr. Garrett stated that the draft agreement is part of the Commission‚Äôs packet. The
agreement is something that Barnes & Thornburg is comfortable with. Representation
from Barnes & Thornburg is present. Staff has also utilized Crowe Horwath as the
accounting firm. This is an agreement that they are also comfortable with. Mr. Boyn has
been involved intimately with the discussions throughout the last couple of months. Mr.
Eldridge has been able to pop in and out as time permitted with some of these
discussions.
Mr. Eash referenced that the company shall not later than December 31, 2014 invest
and complete the project. If they do not meet the deadline, will Thompson Thrift pay
back the full public investment? Or just the Class A bonds and loan?
Mr. Boyn replied that it pays back the Class A bonds and the $1.5 million dollar loan.
The Class B bonds, the City has no obligation to pay anything on if it is not completed
and TIF revenue generated.
Mr. Eash stated that the start dates were going to be earlier, were there issues with the
tenants or something? How is that going?

4

Mr. Boyd replied that Thompson Thrift is working very diligently to secure those
commitments and as indicated they are at their mercy for how fast they move. There
has been a small delay but that was to be anticipated because as a developer that can
happen. Thompson Thrift want to make sure that they have a little bit of flexibility in here
to make sure that they are getting the right tenants and the right structures in place. The
driving factor is to make sure that this project is completed in time for the tax increment
to be in place and established by the end of 2014.
Mr. Eash asked if there were any possibility of further delays. Mr. Boyd replied that he
hopes not. They are going to push this really as hard as they can. Once they are able to
secure the agreement with the City they will be able to move forward.
Mr. Eash said he was tremendously excited at first, but he wants to make sure that it

Eash would like to see this project completed and wrapped up.
Mr. Boyd said right now for Thompson Thrift it is money out the door for them. This is a
very costly venture for them.
Mr. Eash said this has been a long time for the City also.
Mr. Boyd said he is confident they will get things completed.
Mr. Eldridge asked Mr. Boyn to go through the timetable on the funding. Mr. Boyn stated
that the City is not going to fund anything until 75% of the leases are in place. At that
point, the bonding will take place and the loan will take place.
Ms. Paolillo concurred with Mr. Eash thinking that she would hope that things will get
going as Mr. Boyd has explained, with no more delays.

b) 212 Jefferson Development Agreement
Ms. Welsh stated that at the last meeting the Redevelopment Commission approved Mr.
Boyn and Ms. Welsh working on getting the documents in place so that they can move
ahead with the $50,000 loan for DEI to acquire and renovate the property at 212
Jefferson Street. The four documents that Mr. Boyn had to create to make that work are
in the Commission‚Äôs packets.
There is a resolution and development agreement that indicates all of the details
associated with the project. The responsibilities of the City and the responsibilities of the
developer (DEI). There is a promissory note which sets forth the terms for the
repayment of a portion of the loan and a warranty mortgage which puts us in a title
5

position so that we do not run into a problem with having the house lost without us
knowing about it. It puts us in a second lien position after the primary lender which is
Inova Federal Credit Union.
Ms. Welsh stated that the Commission will be providing $50,000. It is from a fund that is
proceeds from sale of Redevelopment Commission properties. It isn‚Äôt directly tied to the
TIF dollars that the Commission see in the TIF budget for downtown TIF, but it is in that
area.
The second thing is given the fact that the property needs significant renovation and
cash flow after the project is a bit in question. Staff is not sure how the units are going to
rent. They are hoping that the community is excited about the project and that DEI gets
some good quality tenants in there and they can charge a reasonable rent. To insure
that that happens, staff has decided to give them two years to kind of figure that out and
at the end of two years, they should have a pretty much stabilized operating budget for
the project. Any repayment of that $50,000 would be based on pretty much an excess of
what they need to actually operate the building. In the promissory note it indicates a 1.4
debt coverage ratio which gives them enough funds to actually meet their operating
expenses, their debt payments, their other issues that they have to operate the building
and a little bit of a cushion. Staff does not want them to run exactly at zero zero. We
need to make sure they have funds available to do renovations or if they have a unit
that needed to be renovated after a tenant left. We want to make sure that they are
operating the building in a good way.
After that two year mark, we will evaluate their actual operating expenses and their
revenues and decide what a reasonable payment will be on that $50,000 mortgage. Ms.
Welsh said if it would have gone by itself without the City‚Äôs help, we would have loved
that. This project is one of those, like many downtown, that needs a subsidy to make
them work. This is very similar to the concept that we worked out at 214 Division
project. Let the market tell us what this property is worth and that will determine what
subsidy we need. We do not want to over subsidize the projects we want projects that
are going to be successful, but we also understand that these projects would not occur
without the subsidy from the City.
Mr. Eldridge asked if Ms. Welsh was comfortable with the fact that $50,000 would be
enough to do the renovation. Ms. Welsh said that is what the experts has told her. Mr.
Eldridge said his concern is that we had these things in the past where we put out
$50,000 to get the project off the ground and then we find out it is going to take another
$50,000 to get it done. Mr. Eldridge is just wondering how much due diligence has been
done at this point to make sure we are reasonably in the ballpark.
Ms. Welsh said that we have representatives from the developer (DEI) present, Mr. Dan
Boecher and Mr. Mike Huber to answer those questions.
Mr. Boecher replied to Mr. Eldridge‚Äôs question. This is something that collectively the
Board does have some experience in doing single family, multi family and some
6

commercial renovations. The amount is different for every property but going in there
and seeing what you have to work with there are some good things you have to work
with that are not present in some giant total gut rehab. This is not something that will
necessarily take down to the studs. There components of that that will be reused. There
will not be a ton of construction because it is actually already set up as a multi family
property. They will not be changing the structure too much. The unknowns, while there
is always some, Mr. Boecher is very confident that while it is not too much certainly
there are ample funds there to be able to get the project done in the condition with what
they want to have it at the end. Obviously at the end of the project DEI will sit down with
staff showing the cost that they had, insurance, etc. and go through it. It is all open
book. They would like the Commission to have confidence in them and they want to be
good stewards of the public funds that we are talking about here and appreciate the
flexibility that the Commission is demonstrating and the recognition. The risk is on the
front end and DEI does not want to over subsidize it but they also recognize that they
are going out projections for the rents, vacancies, expenses etc.
Ms. Welsh said the other portion is that the Commission would be providing the funds to
Inova who will act as escrow agent for this construction process. There will be a series
of draws against those funds and that the Inova funds are set at $25,000. The City
funds will only be used up to $50,000. If the project comes in under budget, then they
will actually only be borrowing the amount of funds they need to complete the project. It
is not a set $50,000. If it will come in slightly under budget, those savings will be seen in
the City‚Äôs portion of that.
Mr. Eldridge asked if the staff would be approving the draws. Ms. Welsh replied that
staff would trust Inova‚Äôs escrow agents to do that. DEI will need to provide proof that
that the work is done, signed and released from the contractors. Staff is talking about
making sure we have lien waivers so that they can‚Äôt come back and do a mechanics lien
at a later date on the property. Mr. Boyn and Ms. Welsh have discussed this and they
feel comfortable because Inova does this kind of thing frequently and they are set up to
act as escrow agent for construction loans.
Mr. Boyn stated that DEI is going to have a licensed architect lined up to review the
work as it is being done and confirmed to Inova and DEI that the contractor has
performed up to the point they are asking for reimbursement.
Ms. Paolillo asked where is this property. Ms. Welsh replied that 212 Jefferson is about
1 ¬Ω blocks north on Jefferson Street. The reason staff is particularly interested in it is
because the Commission owns 209 North Second Street which is an NSP 3 project and
the properties abut each other in the rear. By stabilizing this property as well as the one
we are investing in, we are hoping that we can build a little momentum just two blocks
north of us here and really start to revitalize that neighborhood.
Ms. Paolillo asked how many units are there. Ms. Welsh replied that 209 North Second
Street will be a six unit building and 212 Jefferson will be either a duplex or three unit

7

building. It is currently designed as a three unit and we are trying to work to figure out
whether it makes sense to leave it that way or go for a duplex.
Mr. Eash asked if this was a loan that they will have to pay back, is it forgivable. Ms.
Welsh said the loan is based on the net operating budget. After month 25, DEI will start
to pay us something back based on the revenues that the property is generating. It is
likely that they will not receive the full $50,000 back, but the intent is that the
Commission will receive a portion of those funds back based on the revenues
generated from the project itself.
Mr. Eldridge stated that the provisions state that DEI will have to hold onto the property
for ten years. Mr. Boyn said that DEI cannot resale the property for two years. If they do
resale it, they will have to pay the Commission back with the monies that were
generated from the sale.
Mr. Boyn said if they sell the property for less, then the City would have to agree to take
whatever the amount is that would be less than the full payoff.
After further discussion, Mr. Eash made a motion to approve the funding and content of
the agreement as presented by Ms. Welsh, seconded by Ms. Paolillo; motion carried.
Mr. David Henke stated that the concern he has had is that he has heard several things
even though the Commission is different than the Council. It is concerning when we
have such an investment in a consolidated area that we must invest more to stabilize
our own investment. Secondly, we always skew the markets. It is always these funds
going in, how do private investors compete with those investors that are getting
subsidized. It is a matter that if $50,000 was to be paid back over the ten years, Mr.
Henke would have no problem with this whatsoever, but as an investor/developer
himself, he has to go to the bank and sign his own business plan and a project that
supports the revenue coming in. He can‚Äôt go through the City because that would tell
him this project does not bear its own weight. It does not have the ROI necessary
without City action; therefore it seems as though sometimes through grants, state funds,
and taxes nonetheless, we are subsidizing at a great cost a surplus of housing.
Mr. Henke stated that he is not sure if Elkhart needs more rental housing. He is a rental
provider, as well as Councilman Osborne, but they are both competing with projects
such as this. Both trying to find stable tenants to stabilize their properties, yet competing
with those that are getting subsidized and forgivable loans. It gets to be concerning. Not
all properties are worth refurbishing, Mr. Henke would suppose. A project, if the market
demand is there, the payback ought to be there without a forgivable loan. Nonetheless,
there is a surplus of housing and a surplus of rental properties which devalues all of us.

f) NSP Land Bank Resolution
Ms. Welsh reported that the Commission over the last four years has been acquiring
properties under the NSP 1 and NSP 3 programs for the purpose of land banking. Staff
has been taking these properties, removing a blighted structure. Land banking is a
technique to consolidate properties and put them back on the market more slowly. Over
time the NSP land banks are both set up for 10 years. At that point the City does have
to dispose of the property. Hopefully it won‚Äôt take that long to do it, but under the NSP
rules they do have to be disposed of within ten years.
Staff has been managing the land bank properties. They just decided that it was about
time that they actually formally place them into land bank so that if for reason somebody
was actually interested in buying one of these, they will understand that there are some
infringements on that and how the property can be reused because of the NSP
program.
Ms. Welsh wanted to kind of formalize that so if anybody tried to pull title if they were

ROLL CALL
Ms. Stevens: I would like to call the June 13, 2013 meeting of the Area Plan
Commission of Evansville and Vanderburgh County to order. Will the secretary please
call the roll?
Members Present:
H. Dan Adams, Marty Amsler, Dewey Colter, Lynn Lowe, Stephen Melcher, Jeffrey

APPROVAL OF MINUTES
Ms. Stevens: Is there a motion to approve the May minutes? (Motion was made and
seconded.) The minutes of the May meeting are approved.
REZONINGS
Ms. Stevens: For rezonings, it takes seven affirmative votes to recommend approval of
a petition or seven negative votes to recommend denial of a petition. In the event that
there are not seven votes, it still goes forward to the City Council or County Commission
with no recommendation.
The Area Plan Commission has established the following guidelines to be followed for
both rezonings and subdivisions. Mr. London will begin each presentation. As each
case is called, the petitioner and the remonstrators who intend to testify will please
stand and be sworn in at the beginning of the process. If your name is not on the

Area Plan Commission
June 13, 2013
Page 2

petition, those who plan to testify need to please fill out the sheets in the back of the
room. All testimony must begin by stating your name and address for the record.
The petitioner or person appearing for the case being heard will have a maximum of 10
minutes for the presentation of evidence, statements, and arguments in support of the
petition. Then there will be a total of 10 minutes for the remonstrators. This testimony
will be followed by a five minute rebuttal period for the petitioner as a summation of the
case. Any request for additional time must be voted on by the Board. A timer will be
used to help enforce the time limits. Both petitioners and remonstrators should organize
their testimony to adhere to these guidelines.
When there is a group of individuals remonstrating against a petition, we strongly
encourage the group to designate a spokesperson. If it is necessary for more than one
remonstrator to speak, the group should meet out in the hall before the Area Plan
Commission discussion of the agenda item, to coordinate the information presented, so
that each speaker addresses a different issue of concern. In order to expedite the
meeting, remonstrators should refrain from repeating the same concerns already
expressed by another speaker about a particular development proposal. The Plan
Commission appreciates the cooperation of all participants with these guidelines.
If the Commissioners have questions about issues that we feel have not been
sufficiently addressed by the applicant, we have the option to request a continuance
until the information needed to sufficiently answer our concerns is available or provided
by the applicant or technical staff.
The city rezonings considered today will be heard at the City Council meeting on
Monday, July 8, 2013 at 5:30 p.m. in Room 301. The county rezoning considered today
will be heard at the County Commission meeting on Tuesday, July 9, 2013 at 5:30 p.m.
in Room 301.
Now let‚Äôs move on to the first petition on the agenda.
Mr. Stahl: Mr. London, on all matters before the Board, do you swear or affirm that the
testimony you will give is true and accurate so help you God? (Mr. London has been
sworn in.)

Area Plan Commission

This house is in a predominantly residential area of older homes on very small lots.

request to downzone this M-3 zoned site to bring the existing residence into
conformance with zoning code restrictions and to remove the legal nonconforming

This downzoning to R-2 is consistent with the adjacent residential neighborhood

adequate on-site parking for commercial or industrial use of the site difficult. The
Comprehensive Plan designates this area for mixed use which includes residential,
commercial, and industrial development. The site is in an older area of very mixed use,
predominantly industrial to the west of Grove Street and predominantly residential use

industrial use since the 1940‚Äôs. Most of the residences in the surrounding blocks are
also zoned industrial. This downzoning to R-2 is consistent with the Comprehensive
Plan and the existing residential use.

Appeals for all electronic message boards and/or signs with flashing, moving, rotating or
intermittent lights, or animated messages. Special Use # 13 is permitted with BZA
approval only in commercial or industrial districts. The applicant proposes a new
electronic message sign for the church along the Millersburg Road frontage. This is a
request for C-1 zoning to allow the church to file for the BZA electronic sign special use.

sign. The small size of the rezoning area will limit the size of the proposed new sign.
The existing church on this site is located on the north side of Millersburg Road,
between Hedden and Newbury Roads. Access exists on the site as was approved by

visibility for egress onto Millersburg Road. Staff will address compliance with all code
requirements upon submission of plans for the erection of the new sign on the site.
After approval of the rezoning of the site for the sign, the church must file application for
SU-13 approval for erection of the new electronic sign, to be heard by the Board of
Zoning Appeals.

SUBDIVISIONS
Ms. Stevens: The rezoning portion of the meeting is now over and we will now hear
the proposed subdivisions that are on our agenda. As stated earlier, the Area Plan
Commission is the sole authority on subdivisions. State law and our Subdivision
Control Ordinance dictate the issues the Plan Commission can consider when reviewing
a subdivision application. Unlike a rezoning, consideration of a subdivision is limited to
whether it complies with the standards and requirements in the local Subdivision Control
Ordinance. If a subdivision application meets the requirements set forth in the
Subdivision Control Ordinance, the Area Plan Commission must approve the primary
plat. Indiana Courts have indicated that Plan Commissions have no discretion in this
regard, and that our role in reviewing and acting on subdivisions is purely ministerial.
Seven affirmative votes are needed to approve a subdivision plat and conversely, seven
negative votes are required to deny a plat. In the event that there are not seven votes
for or against, this is considered a no action vote and the plat returns to the next APC
meeting for consideration.
The guidelines for testimony on subdivisions will be the same as those explained at the
onset of this meeting. Petitioners and remonstrators should remember that the only
testimonies the APC can consider are facts that prove whether the plat complies with
the specific standards in the Subdivision Control Ordinance. Copies of the Subdivision
Control Ordinance are available in the Area Plan Commission office in Room 312 or on
our website at evansvilleapc.com.
Now let‚Äôs move on to the subdivisions.
1-S-2013 Enclave at Eagle Creek
Section 29 T6S/R11W Perry Township Map #CO-65 Lot(s): 67
Location: Located on Felstead Road, south of W Lloyd Expressway.
Mr. London: The Enclave at Eagle Creek revised plat is a 60-lot residential and
commercial subdivision located on a 22.7-acre site west of Felstead Road and south of
Lloyd Expressway. On February 14, 2013, the Area Plan Commission granted primary plat
approval for the original 66-lot version of this subdivision. The northern 3.82 acres of this
property was rezoned from Ag to C-4 with a Use & Development Commitment by the County
Commissioners on March 12, 2013. This area for commercial development was part of the
original plat and was proposed as 13 smaller lots originally (designed for home sites). The
revised plat now shows this area as 3 lots (presumably for commercial development). The
public streets that were planned to extend through the area have been removed from the plat,
eliminating one of the two public subdivision entrances on Felstead Road. This change in the
plat requires review by the APC. The Subdivision Review Committee reviewed the plat

Area Plan Commission
June 13, 2013
Page 8

revisions on May 14, 2013. The plat shows an eastern subdivision entrance on Felstead

Road at Cliftwood Drive, and a second western access at Stellar Drive near the Eagle
Village Apartments. The subdivision streets extend from these access points into the
site and connect to the internal subdivision road network. If a commercial entrance on
Lot 57 is planned within the INDOT right-of-way line on Felstead Road at the northern
end of the site, this access will require INDOT approval. Sidewalks are required by
Code.
Comments on the revised plat from the County Engineer indicate the following :
-

-

Erosion control measures will be especially important due to the extensive
grading anticipated and steep grades on the site.
Any driveways on Felstead Road within Lot 57 and north of the line marked L5
on the plat will require INDOT approval.
Utility or drainage pipes under any existing roads must be bored instead of open
cut trenching.
Concerns about sight distance stemming from the curvature and grade of
Felstead, and the embankment on the west side of road at the Felstead Road /
Cliftwood Dr. intersection.
Removal of the classified forest designation for Lots 38, 39 and 40.
Determine sidewalk alignment to connect the existing sidewalk along Stellar
Drive with Felstead Road, and meet all ADA sidewalk requirements.

The Evansville MPO comments also addressed the need for sidewalks to connect this
development with Stellar Drive to the west so that the area will have pedestrian
accessibility to the METS USI Bus route on Schutte Road and to the USI campus. Two
of their other recommendations were comments on the original plat, but were only
slightly changed to reflect lot renumbering on the revised plat.
Comments from INDOT require that any connection to Felstead Road (within the INDOT
right-of-way) will need INDOT approval and submittal of a Traffic Impact Study for the
development plan. City water and sewer are available by extension at the site. A letter
of credit is required. The Water and Sewer Department comments state that the existing
water line might need to be relocated for Lots 1-5 (this water line continues through Lot
50). The required easements need to be granted on the plat from the approved utility
plans. The preliminary drainage plan was approved for the revised Enclave at Eagle
Cliff subdivision by the County Drainage Board on April 23, 2013. The required
drainage easements must be shown on the plat prior to recording. If the Enclave at
Eagle Cliff subdivision is approved, primary plat approval should include the conditions
listed in the staff field report.

primary plat totaling 55 lots. These two sections access through the residential
subdivisions to the east. The primary plat for Poet square also shows an access to the
west of the subdivision on Peck Road. In the primary subdivision approval, the Area

Area Plan Commission
June 13, 2013
Page 10

Plan Commission placed an access condition on this plat as allowed by State law,
based on comments about the original plat from the County Engineer and the EMPO.
The condition states that ‚ÄúAccess to Peck Road should not be allowed until the roadway
is improved to a standard two-lane facility from Baseline Road to Old State Road.‚Äù The
road was widened south of the North High and Middle School entrance, which is the
southern half of the road segment specified in the condition. The County recently
resurfaced the road north of the school entrance and added an approximate two-foot
rock shoulder and a section of guard rail. However, this portion of Peck Road‚Äôs
pavement has not been widened from its original size.
The applicant now requests to eliminate the condition on the primary plat approval
restricting access to Peck Road until it is widened. The proposed subdivision street to
access Peck Road (Road # 6 on the primary plat) is highlighted in the picture shown on
your screens and will connect to Peck near the southwest corner of the primary plat.
The existing access to the two sections of Poet Square that have been recorded is a
westward extension of the existing Natalie Drive into the site from the Chadwick Place
subdivision adjacent to the east.
The APC members have been provided a copy of the County Engineer‚Äôs comments on
the proposed removal of the access condition. Due to safety concerns about the
inadequate width of Peck Road, the County Engineer is not in favor of allowing access
to Peck until it is widened from North High School to Baseline Road. His conclusion is
that Peck Road cannot accommodate additional traffic at its current width. The recent
resurfacing and guardrail improvements to the narrow portion of the road have not
changed the safety concerns about the width of the pavement. Vanderburgh County
plans to reconstruct this road in the future, but no schedule has been determined for the
project and no work will occur until TIF funds accumulate to be able to pay for the
upgrade.
Evansville MPO‚Äôs comments on the original primary plat agree with the County
Engineer and state the following: Peck Road (north of the North High School entrance)
is currently of substandard geometry. Peck Road narrows to 14 feet at the drainage
culvert just north of the proposed development. Peck Road is functionally classified as a
local road and therefore would not have access to federal aid for needed improvements.
There are currently no plans and no funding for improvements north to Baseline Road.
We would expect approximately 1800 vehicle trips per day from this development (at
buildout).
Access to Peck Road should be allowed only after the roadway is improved to a
standard two-lane facility from Baseline Road to Old State Road. The access limitation
recommended by the County Engineer and the EMPO will result in Poet Square
temporarily having only one access through the Chadwick Place and Kingsmont
Subdivisions to eventually reach Old State Road. The County Engineer indicated that it
could take about 5 years for enough money to build up in the Highway 41 North TIF to
complete the improvements needed to Peck Road, and that assumes all the TIF funds
generated would be dedicated to the Peck Road project over this period. Based on the

Area Plan Commission
June 13, 2013
Page 11

County Engineer and EMPO comments, staff recommends that the condition of
approval and the corresponding plat note on the access restriction to Peck Road remain
on the plat to protect public safety on this narrow road. The subdivision access to Peck
should be installed once Peck is widened to a standard two-lane facility, giving the
development a second access option.

Mr. Murphy: My name is Brian Murphy, 15401 Haiku Road, Evansville. I‚Äôm the
managing partner of New Urban Investments who is the developer of this real estate.
Does anybody have any questions of me before I start my presentation to convince you
all that we should remove the condition upon the property? Okay. This is just a plat of
the subdivision. INAUDIBLE-AWAY FROM MIC‚Ä¶‚Ä¶ This is at Old State Road and this
is looking north up Peck Road. So this is basically a video of traveling north on Peck

the area where we are assuming is substandard geometry. There is the roadway
guardrails on the right. The video will stop where our entrance and exit will end up
being accessing Peck Road, which is right there. So I think one of the areas probably
everybody has an issue with, there is a bridge as you travel further north that actually
compresses traffic a little bit more which creates a yielding effect between the vehicles
that travel through there. Here is the bridge. You can see the yellow highlighting the
sides of the bridge. I think it is actually approximately 14-15 feet. This is just a bigger
blown up picture. I was anticipating having a laser pointer here. Peck Road obviously
from Google maps, the north complex. Here‚Äôs our site as it relates to the rest. Where
we were at in that previous picture is approximately right here heading north into that
bridge geometry. Here is a video of two vehicles actually crossing through that bridge
area. The bridge way we are referring to is approximately here where this video will be
taking place at. That‚Äôs the narrowest that it gets there. Vehicles somewhat yielding.
The one moving through. I think you saw them both on the bridge where they passed.
So essentially what the claim is is that this road is unsafe for standard two-lane traffic.
But my contention is that it is actually helpful that these measures are on this road, that
it actually slows traffic down. Okay. That it is a calming effect. You will see, I have an
example from another County road. So Mohr Road basically does the same thing, even
to a greater extent because you cannot drive two vehicles through that road. Everybody
know where Mohr Road ends up at? Spring Lake Valley, 142 lot subdivision passed
with no restrictions, no conditions put on it. At buildout, 142 lots. Poet Square 131.
Has the same similar geometry that Mohr Road does. Any questions? This picture
here, this is a design technique utilized by traffic engineers, urban planners, city
planners, that actually, their effect again is to calm traffic. They actually put the yield
point in to force cars to yield as they move through. The idea is not to speed traffic up,
which is what two-lane standard facility geometries do. Wherever you go, sometimes
they say that it doesn‚Äôt increase, it is for traffic congestion. But what ends up
happening, everybody drives on that road and it gets more congested. Well, when what

Area Plan Commission
June 13, 2013
Page 12

used to be a slow, country lane, all of a sudden becomes this wide country highway with
curb, gutter, oversized lanes. High school kids traveling down it, what do they do?
They speed up. So again, both instances those cars were doing something that the
road is making them to do. They are not being told. There is no signage to say stop.
There is no flashing signs. There is no traffic engineer telling them. There are actually
studies that correlate speeds and road widths to increased accidents, increased
fatalities. One of those studies, residential street topology and injury accident frequency
done by an engineer, actually out of Longmont, Colorado. He makes the point that the
safest residential streets are 24 feet or less. You can say, this isn‚Äôt a residential street.
It is either an arterial or a collector. Okay, I‚Äôm moving to traffic counts now. When we
started talking about the kind of traffic counts that are going to be affecting this road.
This is from back in October, a 48-hour period. So I just took both lanes because they
actually put a counter on either end of the road, one southbound and northbound.
Added those together. 1,447 cars. That‚Äôs in 48 hours. Compare that with Mohr Road
from 2008, that data I collected was AADTC. That was only 24 hours but I just doubled
it to come up with the 2,598. Remember, that‚Äôs 2008 data. So I am only going to
assume there is more traffic on that road today than there was in 2008. Just some
general comments on potential case law issues, the denial of the Peck use substantially
devalues the land at Poet Square resulting in a taking without compensation, violation of
Fifth Amendment of the US Constitution Article 1, Sec. 21. And in fact, Indiana Supreme
Court has recognized that ingress and egress to and from a public highway is a public
right and cannot be substantially or materially interfered with without due compensation.
Land owners suffer damage that is particular rather than that suffered by the general
public, a taking may be found to have occurred. The County cannot impose a severe
restriction on real estate which devalues the real estate just because the County has not
accepted the responsibility to improve said public road. The denial of the use of Peck
Road by devaluing Poet Square is also illegal or an exaction, roughly requirements that
provide the party to give up something in favor of the public need. But by public law,
exaction needs to be related both in nature and extent of the impact of the developer.
In this case, the overwhelming impact to Peck Road resulted in the construction of
North High School and subsequent school bus traffic generated as a result thereof, not
the development of the subdivision. Supreme Court has held INAUDIBLE‚Ä¶ by the
government and those interests to be served. In this case, the public interest is that
Peck Road should be improved and prohibiting Poet Square from accessing the public
road does nothing further that interest. Five counties allowed other developments on
less than standards shows unequal treatment and also a violation of the constitution.
So I would encourage the removal of this condition.

Ms. Stevens: We have a motion and second. Call the roll.
Mr. Pedtke: (During roll call.) I think it‚Äôs not going to be less safe. I think the traffic can
come from the same subdivision, drive up and down Peck Road. I agree with Dr. Adams
and I vote yes.

Area Plan Commission
June 13, 2013
Page 21

Ayes: Mr. Mueller, Mr. Pedtke, Mr. Rutledge, Mr. Swaim, Dr. Adams, Mr. Amsler, Ms.
Lowe, Ms. Stevens
Nays: Mr. Colter
Abstention: Mr. Melcher
There being 8 affirmative votes, 1 negative vote and 1 abstention, the request is
approved.
Ms. Stevens: I would like to thank Ron again for a great job.
Meeting adjourned.

_________________________________
Stacy Stevens, President
